<div id="review_2340698159" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2340698159" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24437998-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479868929p2/24437998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2340698159?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/24437998-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18622302-city-of-bohane">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24437998-paul?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2340698159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14297539283337611391"> City of Bohane takes place 40 years in the future, in a fictional Irish town by the name of Bohane. Some kind of socioeconomic calamity has taken place and the 'distant' past is referred to as "the lost times". It's unclear exactly what has transpired to bring Bohane to it's knees, but all indications are that it was something, as i say, of an economic collapse. The result is that the town is largely run by several gangs that coexist in a fragile detente. Law and order is largely impotent and r</span>
  <span id="freeText14297539283337611391" style="display:none"> City of Bohane takes place 40 years in the future, in a fictional Irish town by the name of Bohane. Some kind of socioeconomic calamity has taken place and the 'distant' past is referred to as "the lost times". It's unclear exactly what has transpired to bring Bohane to it's knees, but all indications are that it was something, as i say, of an economic collapse. The result is that the town is largely run by several gangs that coexist in a fragile detente. Law and order is largely impotent and redundant. But things are coming to a crisis point as the leaders of the various factions are aging and the youngsters are getting frisky.<br /><br /> The almost (at times), inpenetrable 'Oirish' slang make this heavy going at first, but in short order one comes to understand, through the author's deft use of context, the meaning of even the most obscure terms. It gives the story an authenticity that might otherwise be lacking and at times lends a grim humour to what at times is a brutal recital of violence and mayhem.<br /><br />Quote;<br /> Jenni Ching was on her hands and knees, with her slender rump in the air, and a brass herb-pipe clamped in her gob. She cast over her shoulder a bored glance at the Gant. He looked as if his heart might at any moment explode. His face was purpled, blotched, sweaty.<br /> "If y'wanna take five," she said, jus' holler."<br /> The mocking tone was too much for him, was too delicious, and the Gant spent himself. He fell onto his back and was ashamed then. His heart was a rabid pit bull loose inside his chest.<br /> Jenni Ching consulted the wall clock.<br /> "Three minutes even," she said. "You're comin' on, kid."<br /><br />and;<br /> Bohane was thrun down, as we say, with winter.<br /> Oh give us a grim Tuesday of December, with the hardwind taking schleps at our heads, and the rain coming slantways off that hideous fucking ocean, and the grapes nearly frozen off us, and the dirty ice caked up top of the puddles, and we are not happy, exactly, but satisfied in our despair. <br /><br /> Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14297539283337611391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1988808916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1988808916" />
    <a title="Krista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4729639-krista"><img alt="Krista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579967825p2/4729639.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1988808916?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista" href="/user/show/4729639-krista">Krista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729639-krista?shelf=irishfic">irishfic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729639-krista?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1988808916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5493231800504385270"><i>
  <blockquote>Whatever's wrong with us is coming in off that river. No argument: the taint of badness in the city's air is a taint off that river. This is the Bohane river we're talking about. A blackwater surge, malevolent, it roars in off the Big Nothin' wastes and the city was spawned by it and was named for it: city of Bohane.</blockquote>
</i><br/>Set in a near-future (2053), vaguely post-apocalyptic fictional city on Ireland's west coast, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10277268.City_of_Bohane' title='City of Bohane by Kevin Barry' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Bohane</a> is fueled by sex, drugs, and gang violence, written in language gorge</span>
  <span id="freeText5493231800504385270" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>Whatever's wrong with us is coming in off that river. No argument: the taint of badness in the city's air is a taint off that river. This is the Bohane river we're talking about. A blackwater surge, malevolent, it roars in off the Big Nothin' wastes and the city was spawned by it and was named for it: city of Bohane.</blockquote>
</i><br />Set in a near-future (2053), vaguely post-apocalyptic fictional city on Ireland's west coast, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10277268.City_of_Bohane" title="City of Bohane by Kevin Barry" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Bohane</a> is fueled by sex, drugs, and gang violence, written in language gorgeously inventive, and while it was a fun and interesting read in the moment, it amounts to little more in the end than the “wisps of steam like spectral maggots (that) rose from their damp coats in the inn's fuggyheat”. I kept waiting for the <i>point</i> of this book – perhaps some explanation for the lost-time years that led to this bizarre society; an explanation that would then lay bare some truth of humanity, as the great books do – but there's nothing below the surface here: this is like a very clever language experiment that delights only at the sentence-level. But oh, those sentences do delight.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Hear this!” Ol' Boy cried. “Bohane city don't always gots to be a gang-fight story. We can give 'em a good aul' tangle o' romance an' all, y'check me?”</blockquote>
</i><br />There's something quite surreal about <i>City of Bohane</i>, and perhaps there's an unwritten rule to surrealism that one shouldn't ever explain; never attempt to make the vision plausible. This is only forty years (from the time of the book's publication) into Ireland's future, but most technology has been wiped out (there are jukeboxes and record players but no television; knives but not guns; trains but no cars), the political system is anarchic (with a gang, or Fancy, ruling the bowl of the city and maintaining Calm with the rival factions in the surrounding hills and the near-savages on the beach), the religious zealots pray to “Sweet Baba Jay on the cross”, people listen and dance to calypso music as though it's a secret <i>lingua franca</i>, and the gangbangers dress like dandies. <u>None</u> of this is explained except for some vague references to the lost-years and some reel-to-reel films that show the streets of Bohane once bustling with cars – this <u>is</u> our own world, but somehow, lost. We're promised a good aul' tangle o' romance, so let's meet Logan, leader of the Hartnett Fancy:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>He had that Back Trace look to him: a dapper buck in a natty-boy Crombie, the Crombie draped all casual-like over the shoulders of a pale grey Eyetie suit, mohair. Mouth of teeth on him like a vandalised graveyard but we all have our crosses. It was a pair of hand-stitched Portuguese boots that slapped his footfall, and the stress that fell, the emphasis, was money.</blockquote>
</i><br />Logan has been devotedly married to Macu (for Immaculata; an Iberian beauty whose wonky eye everyone fetishises) for twenty-five years, and the man he stole her from – the Gant, who used to head the Fancy – is rumoured to have returned to the city.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>The Gant's humours were in rum condition – he was about fit for a bleed of leeches. His moods were too swift on the turn. He was watchful of them. He had a sack of tawny wine on him. He untwisted its cap and took a pull on it for the spurt of life – medicinal. There was pikey blood in the Gant, of course – the name, even, was an old pikey handle – but then there's pikey blood in most of us around this city. Have a sconce at the old gaatch of us – the slope-shouldered carry, the belligerence of the stride, the smokey hazel of our eyes; officer material we are not. Of course if you were going by the reckoning of pikey bones the Gant was old bones now for certain. He was fifty years to paradise.</blockquote>
</i><br />Not only does Logan need to deal with old jealousies, but the clans in the hills are spoiling for a fight, and as young folks are wont to do – as he himself had done a quarter century earlier – Logan's lieutenants are plotting their own takeover of the Fancy. Seemingly besieged, Logan proposes a Feud (which is a formal declaration, written in his ninety-year-old mother, Girly's, “mannish” hand and delivered to the rival leader on foot), and Eyes Cusack accepts by handing over a ceremonial receipt (in this case, a drawing of a stick-figure man with genitals growing out of his forehead). As the hilltop clans begin their war-drumming and light huge bonfires encircling the bowl of Bohane, the temper in the city becomes frenzied and anticipatory:<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>He always enjoyed the eve of a Feud. He knew that Eyes Cusack would not for long keep his mongrels leashed, and his mood was high and expectant. When you were running a Fancy, regular demonstrations of rage were needed to keep the town in check, and just as importantly, the Fancy boys in trim. Too much sweetness and light and they got fat, unpleasantly smiley and over-interested in the fashion mags.</blockquote>
</i><br />This isn't actually the climax of the book, but there is much reefing committed with shkelpers, against Fancy, Cusack, and pikey alike, and factions and alliances are regrouped and redrawn; paving the way for the actual climax. This occurs at the August Fair – when the summer heat draws in an obscuring Murk from the nearby ocean – and the narrative is suddenly told in jump scenes: a fat and blind old madame sings a dirge; a feral goat is chosen and raised on a platform for sacrifice; the clickheels on a Fancy's boots trace a route over the cobblestoned wynds; Girly rises from her bed and gets dressed to go out for the first time in decades; the hoss polis face down the sand-pikeys; jump; jump; jump. The action culminates in a satisfying ending, but then...it's over and nothing has been learned. The action has all been for its own sake.<br /><br />I believe in the maxim, “Good books don't make good movies”, and the best thing I can say for <i>City of Bohane</i> is that I think it would make an excellent movie (currently in development). It's all atmosphere and costumes and bloody, sexy action; a steampunk <i>Mad Max</i>; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227463.A_Clockwork_Orange" title="A Clockwork Orange by Anthony Burgess" rel="nofollow noopener">A Clockwork Orange</a> without the message. I picked up this book because it won The International IMPAC Dublin Literary Award for 2013, and I thought that would guarantee a good, literary read. It's not quite that (I don't really understand what the IMPAC jury was thinking here), but I did enjoy this book in the moment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5493231800504385270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/582083246?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/3679784-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781555976453" href="/book/show/16059646-city-of-bohane">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3679784-drew?shelf=favorites-6">favorites-6</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582083246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7535833466625411953">This is just an exceptional piece of writing. The invention never feels forced, never feels overly showy - despite how incredibly showy it might be; the man created an entire slang language, for the sake of the Sweet Baba Jay. Instead, he has breathed life into a story and city as (I daresay) only he could've done. There's sex and fighting and a city as magical as Ambergris and a future that feels both gritty and lovely all at once. If our world tends towards hell, as it very well might, I sure </span>
  <span id="freeText7535833466625411953" style="display:none">This is just an exceptional piece of writing. The invention never feels forced, never feels overly showy - despite how incredibly showy it might be; the man created an entire slang language, for the sake of the Sweet Baba Jay. Instead, he has breathed life into a story and city as (I daresay) only he could've done. There's sex and fighting and a city as magical as Ambergris and a future that feels both gritty and lovely all at once. If our world tends towards hell, as it very well might, I sure hope we at least end up as well dressed as the likes of Jenni Ching and Logan Hartnett and The Gant and Macu. And have a bit of their personalities in the face of such a future, too. <br />This novel shows an author who will, I have no doubt, come to be regarded as one of the very best to've ever bent his pen towards a trembling blank page. It is, again, exceptional. A thing of power and beauty and delightful fancy. His two short story collections are out this month and Bohane is on shelves now. I so very rarely do this - but I implore you, with all speed, to acquire all three. You will not regret it. <br /><br />A full, even more considered, rave to come at RB: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://wp.me/pGVzJ-O5">http://wp.me/pGVzJ-O5</a></span>

<div id="review_363436216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/363436216" />
    <a title="Matthew Geyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8240020-matthew-geyer"><img alt="Matthew Geyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592175410p2/8240020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/363436216?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Geyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Geyer" href="/user/show/8240020-matthew-geyer">Matthew Geyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer363436216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8059830398479857249">Kevin Barry is going to be somebody. That's what I thought when I read his apocalyptic short story in The New Yorker, Fjord of Killary, a year or two ago. This sent me searching the web, where I found his previous short story collection, There Are Little Kingdoms, available from a small Irish literary press by way of an independent overseas bookseller. Kevin Barry already is somebody, I thought when I read those tales: He's an heir to William Trevor, like Banville and Toibin. But this one's ten </span>
  <span id="freeText8059830398479857249" style="display:none">Kevin Barry is going to be somebody. That's what I thought when I read his apocalyptic short story in The New Yorker, Fjord of Killary, a year or two ago. This sent me searching the web, where I found his previous short story collection, There Are Little Kingdoms, available from a small Irish literary press by way of an independent overseas bookseller. Kevin Barry already is somebody, I thought when I read those tales: He's an heir to William Trevor, like Banville and Toibin. But this one's ten or twenty years younger than those, so the line is growing at a natural, Irish pace.<br /><br />In his first novel, published last year in Europe and this year in the US, Barry explores the devolution of western society and culture in a futuristic tale that is anything but science fiction. The language of the book, both the dialogue and the narration, represent what will become of the English language by 2053 if the current course holds. A melange of hip-hop drug-running street-slang wafts through the streets of a fictional coastal town in the West of Ireland, where the polluted Bohane river emerges from the Irish countryside--aka "The Big Nothin', ya sketch?--to flow through the city of the same name to a blackened sea. On the south side of the river, Smoketown is a place of sex parlors and opium dens, all run on graft, young hoors shaved head to toe, and tribal inheritances and alliances soon to be shaken yet again when an old chieftain rolls back into town. Up the slope on the other side of the river, the Northside Rises are home to another nest of criminals and hooligans. In between, what serves as the establishment--even the blue bloods are cynical and uncouth in this land--are soon needing to prepare for the worst. Nary a cell-phone or a laptop or a satellite dish in sight, gang fights and melees are fought with knuckles and knives and old-time savagery. And there is hell to pay, one way or another.<br /><br />Kevin Barry. Check any of it out, including City of Bohane. A young Irish writer of this caliber is a new world treasure.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8059830398479857249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_343031651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343031651" />
    <a title="James Murphy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2422285-james-murphy"><img alt="James Murphy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262206618p2/2422285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343031651?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Murphy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Murphy" href="/user/show/2422285-james-murphy">James Murphy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781555976088" href="/book/show/12231510-city-of-bohane">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343031651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9397714994041514433">The city of Bohane is a rough neighborhood. It's a dystopian city on the west coast of Ireland in a time about 40 years in the future. Its citizens have gone to seed. There's little municipal control or services. Vice reigns as various tribes and chieftains compete for dominance.<br/><br/>As fiction, it's a language novel. If the city isn't the central character the language is. The people of Bohane speak a kind of noir street talk made up of high slang and dialect which carries both the rhythms of Irish </span>
  <span id="freeText9397714994041514433" style="display:none">The city of Bohane is a rough neighborhood. It's a dystopian city on the west coast of Ireland in a time about 40 years in the future. Its citizens have gone to seed. There's little municipal control or services. Vice reigns as various tribes and chieftains compete for dominance.<br /><br />As fiction, it's a language novel. If the city isn't the central character the language is. The people of Bohane speak a kind of noir street talk made up of high slang and dialect which carries both the rhythms of Irish brogue and the Caribbean.<br /><br />The novel isn't so much the story of a person or group. There is a loose narrative. There's conflict, climax, denouement, and result. But the novel's more about the imagined town, Bohane, which is like a rich anarchic stew with characters as ingredients which swirl around and bubble up and down, coming into view as author and reader need them before sinking out of sight again into some thick neighborhood. They're a gallery of underground figures who prowl the city in search of power and whatever's nefarious. This is a slice of Dickens for the 21st century.<br /><br />Sure an' it's a dangerous place, Bohane is, as you plod the eerie streets trying to stay our of the shadows. It's a place for open eyes at all times, but moreso for open ears because the rich language will delight and be your safe guide. Though it's smokey and dark, though the streets seem perpetually wet, there's a music everywhere not generated by pub jukeboxes or radios in the market. It's the reggae babble of the townspeople. It's a babble of fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9397714994041514433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172483025" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172483025" />
    <a title="Linda Anne Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4186988-linda-anne-smith"><img alt="Linda Anne Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308239957p2/4186988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172483025?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda Anne Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda Anne Smith" href="/user/show/4186988-linda-anne-smith">Linda Anne Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172483025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2132054437598620529">This is a book that you will either love or hate. I did both!!! <br/>I read the first 2 chapters and really struggled with them, both in terms of the language (very broad Irish dialect and patois) and also just trying to find something - character or story - to start building the reading experience from. To be honest, if it wasn't for the fact that i "had to" read it for Book Club, I would not have persevered with this book. So I started again, and re-read the beginning, and kept going second-time ar</span>
  <span id="freeText2132054437598620529" style="display:none">This is a book that you will either love or hate. I did both!!! <br />I read the first 2 chapters and really struggled with them, both in terms of the language (very broad Irish dialect and patois) and also just trying to find something - character or story - to start building the reading experience from. To be honest, if it wasn't for the fact that i "had to" read it for Book Club, I would not have persevered with this book. So I started again, and re-read the beginning, and kept going second-time around. However by the time i got about a third of the way through, I realised that the book had hooked me in - at teatime I was just dying for bedtime to get out my book and find out what happened next!!! There was not a specific incident - the book/ plot/ characters just sort of slowly grew in my subconscious, and nobody could have been more surprised by this than me!!! <br />It tells of the struggle for power in a small irish town in the year 2054, and the setting is intensely dark, almost to the point of grotesque, although there is no explanation as to how this civilisation got to this point. There is no technology (phones, laptops, tvs etc) and no government - local or national. There is however a lot of gang warfare.<br />Some people have commented on the lack of storyline. However, I did think there was quite an intricate plot going on between all of the main - and some of the secondary - characters. But in many cases, the author was (quite deliberately i think) not giving the whole game away, but leaving the reader to dot the i's and cross the t's of what was going on. And in some cases he - the author - just left you wondering "why", "what", "how"????? At first, this annoyed me, all these unanswered questions, but then I got to thinking maybe its not such a bad thing, leaving space for the readers' imagination to fill in the gaps e.g. why was there no technology, phones, pcs etc.?? And so when I came to the end, rather than being disappointed, my feelings were more of "ooh, I wonder why" or even "I wonder if"....<br />I did think that there was a bit too much gratuitous sex and violence for my liking, but hey, I know that i'm a bit of a softie re these things!!!<br />Would I recommend it to all my friends - definitely not - but perhaps i would suggest it to one or two, although i'd warn them that it is perhaps a bit of a risky read......</span>
  <a data-text-id="2132054437598620529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>
  </div>
    <div class="elementListBrownSeparator"></div>



  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_379985201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379985201" />
    <a title="T.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1143674-t-r"><img alt="T.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1210134216p2/1143674.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379985201?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.R." href="/user/show/1143674-t-r">T.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379985201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3146585586533053478">As a high school teacher, I'm taking a summer class on on teaching reading and we reviewed a list of the 'pleasures of reading.' And the first two had to do with the pleasure associated with knowing the correspondences between letters and sounds and the pleasure of the sounds themselves as you read aloud. Barry's novel, for all it's atmosphere and impact in the literary circles, reminds me of those first two pleasures. Barry is mostly known as a short story writer, and it shows. On each page the</span>
  <span id="freeText3146585586533053478" style="display:none">As a high school teacher, I'm taking a summer class on on teaching reading and we reviewed a list of the 'pleasures of reading.' And the first two had to do with the pleasure associated with knowing the correspondences between letters and sounds and the pleasure of the sounds themselves as you read aloud. Barry's novel, for all it's atmosphere and impact in the literary circles, reminds me of those first two pleasures. Barry is mostly known as a short story writer, and it shows. On each page the slang, the syntax, the imagery are stunning. Within the first two pages: "There was an evenness to his footfall, a slow calm rhythm of leather on stone... Mouth of teeth on him like a vandalised graveyard but we all have our crosses. It was a pair of hand-stitched Portuguese boots that slap his footfall, and the stress that fell, the emphasis, was money." Listen to this dialogue as two folks in the Hartnett Fancy gang talk about some possible trouble: "Cusacks gonna sulk up a welt o' vengeance by 'n' by and if yer askin' me, like? A rake o' them tossers bullin' down off the Rises is the las' thing Smoketown need." I'll stop writing already. Go read the book.<br /><br />OK, I do want to say something else. The Irish don't have sole proprietorship on nostalgia. Talk to any local in my neighborhood and within in 10 minutes you'll be talking about what the folks in the City of Bohane call the "lost times." You'll be talking about what shop was where, how much a burrito used to cost, and where the best places were for music. For the Irish of Bohane though, the lost times were invariable violent. And the violence gave them a gravity. Yet the violence was rarely remembered for the honesty of loss and was looked forward to mark the passing of time. "y'sure 'bout that, H? 'nother winter a blood in Bohane, like? "Ah sure it'll make the long old nights fly past." <br /><br />The fatalism is felt deep in Bohane. "Whatever's wrong with us is coming in off the river. No argument: the taint of badness on the city's air is a taint off that river." Barry's book is set in the future, but the ideas have a deeper history in Irish literature and culture. And if Barry's plot structure is any indication, things won't be changing much.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3146585586533053478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_306997951" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/306997951" />
    <a title="zxvasdf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2882638-zxvasdf"><img alt="zxvasdf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309066617p2/2882638.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306997951?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="zxvasdf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="zxvasdf" href="/user/show/2882638-zxvasdf">zxvasdf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2882638-zxvasdf?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306997951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17271546907728025203">Bohane, a city on the Irish coast fed by a sick black river, is crime ridden. But... how can we call it crime if it is just a way of life? When everyone is actively engaged in a monstrous caricature of humanity, the dark manifesting in feints of genteel respectability? It's hard to see what value the Bohanites hold upon anything other than irrepressible self indulgence. Smoke and drink and carnality, amongst others is just parts in a day. People are people, they say, but the people of Bohane hav</span>
  <span id="freeText17271546907728025203" style="display:none">Bohane, a city on the Irish coast fed by a sick black river, is crime ridden. But... how can we call it crime if it is just a way of life? When everyone is actively engaged in a monstrous caricature of humanity, the dark manifesting in feints of genteel respectability? It's hard to see what value the Bohanites hold upon anything other than irrepressible self indulgence. Smoke and drink and carnality, amongst others is just parts in a day. People are people, they say, but the people of Bohane have been sucking in the air from the river.<br /><br />There's magic in this book, in which the year of 2053 can seem so... dated. As if it were the early 1900s only the people dress cooler, and the knives are sharper, and the cruelty is more practiced. Honed. It's tomorrow, indeed. Something bad and big happened and the old ways have found to be as sturdy as ever. <br /><br />There's something exceptional about British and Irish writers that somehow imbues the new with an ancient grace; you find the new things never really changed at all, and that the old things can be new again. They live on a ground filled with the ghosts of raw history, and it seeps into everything, especially in the mad minds of writers like Kevin Barry. People talented in sketching out a story in which you are required to peer in the emptiness between plot lines to ken the true happening.<br /><br />This story is not only an aborted love story; it's a passing of the torch tale, the swan song of one dapper gentleman killer. The scales swing and shift as intrigues blows allegiances and confidences like a wynd through the Reaches. The Fancy is a man stumbling about in a maelstrom of events, but so dream-snared as to be consciously blind to it occurring. But it occurs. As he tried not to see it. <br /><br />I've a mind our sly author will find himself, in the decades ahead a fadograph of the lost time, in possession of a cadre of old reel for the most self-indulgent of the wicked, and a voice compelled to yarn a tale of the ill wind that blows off the Big Nothin' on the bad black river Bohane. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17271546907728025203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y1RdWmY52auz1b+ExqJ3g05WJfwiO6dtN7B1HW9PYXG6MXZhCDY8/B9vImShBj00ydew0xm8R1bHScpLR59bQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7M+wi/QezKaVoCWhYtl3h7Oo8AdfwKgALzpCXyqDcmGdqpuwmhEp8TkauEEFfT0wNCllKGRHSDvfw/0JAlNIUw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

There are the Ruttledges, who came from London in search of a different life on the edge of the village lake; John Quinn, who will stop at nothing to ensure a flow of women through his life; Jimmy Joe McKiernan, head of the local IRA as well as town auctioneer and undertaker; the gentle Jamesie and his wife, Mary, who have never left the lake and who know about everything that ever stirred or moved there; Patrick Ryan, the builder who never quite finishes what he starts; Bill Evans, the farmhand whose orphaned childhood was marked with state-sanctioned cruelties and whose adulthood is marked by the scars; and the wealthiest man in town, known as the Shah. \n\nA year in the lives of these and other characters unfolds through the richly observed rituals of work and play, of religious observance and annual festivals, and the details of the changing seasons, of the cycles of birth and death. With deceptive simplicity and eloquence, the author reveals the fundamental workings of human nature as it encounters the extraordinary trials and pleasures, terrors and beauty, of ordinary life.\n\nBy the Lake is John McGahern’s most ambitious, generous, and superbly realized novel yet.\n\n(above copied from amazon.com)<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7599549764913026443\" href=\"#\" They opened a fish-and-chip shop in Acocks Green. The Great Western Fish Bar is where Pete learned about coin-operated machines, male banter and Britishness.Shy and introverted, Pete stopped speaking from age 4 to 7, and found refuge instead in the bittersweet embrace of pop songs, thanks to Top of the Pops and Dial-A-Disc. From Brotherhood of Man to UB40, from ABBA to The Police, music provided the safety net he needed to protect him from the tensions of his home life. It also helped him navigate his way around the challenges surrounding school, friendships and phobias such as visits to the barber, standing near tall buildings and Rod Hull and Emu.With every passing year, his guilty secret became more horrifying to him: his parents were Greek, but all the things that excited him were British. And the engine of that realisation? \'Sugar Baby Love\', \'Don\'t Go Breaking My Heart\', \'Tragedy\', \'Silly Games\', \'Going Underground\', \'Come On Eileen\', and every other irresistibly       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/490256.Kevin_Barry">About Kevin Barry</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/490256.Kevin_Barry"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1439060562p3/490256.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/490256.Kevin_Barry">Kevin Barry
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
573
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8404472097351744352">Kevin Barry is an Irish writer. He is the author of two collections of short stories, and the novel City of Bohane, which was the winner of the 2013 International IMPAC Dublin Literary Award. </span>

</div>
</div>
